<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1732300626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7450716146936754000"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“That's why crazy people are so dangerous. You think they're nice until they're chaining you up in the garage.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>How did I miss this book in life?!?!?! Why did I never even hear about it! Thankfully I have remedied this situation and read the book! <br/><br/>This is what I expect in a great middle-grade novel. This book was well-written, had wonderful characters, great adventure, lots of humor and just an overall good time. I have no clue why I have never heard of this book, but I'm sure glad I</span>
  <span id="freeText7450716146936754000" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“That's why crazy people are so dangerous. You think they're nice until they're chaining you up in the garage.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />How did I miss this book in life?!?!?! Why did I never even hear about it! Thankfully I have remedied this situation and read the book! <br /><br />This is what I expect in a great middle-grade novel. This book was well-written, had wonderful characters, great adventure, lots of humor and just an overall good time. I have no clue why I have never heard of this book, but I'm sure glad I stumbled past it in my library and it caught my eye. I adore <i>The Brothers Grimm</i> so when I saw that name attached to this book it was a no-brainer for me. I knew this book was going to be made just for me.<br /><br />I had no real expectations with this books, since I had never heard of, so it was a very pleasant surprise to read something so great. I was pretty surprised at the humor in this one, it was something that adults could enjoy just as much as kids. There was nothing inappropriate though. I know some children't movies and books have adult jokes in them that can kind of push the line - this wasn't like that. It's completely safe to let your kids read, in my opinion.<br /><br />I'm a sucker for fairy tales and nursery rhyme characters and this had them in abundance. This book is what I was expecting from <i>The Land of Stories</i> but didn't get. I don't think there were any characters that I didn't like and the kids weren't annoying or whiny, which is a plus. They are sisters (hence the title) and their relationship with each other was very believable. Another huge plus for me with this book is that I LOVE that they included Puck in this story, for those who are familiar with that character I'm sure it will bring a smile to your face as well. <br /><br />I would highly recommend this one. If there was a set for sale on the entire series, I would just go ahead and purchase it, that is how impressed I was with this first installment of the series. I will certainly continuing the series. Five stars all the way for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7450716146936754000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2301505369" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2301505369" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2301505369?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2301505369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer218199034604290422">Needing something a little shorter to fit into my reading schedule, I turned to this series debut by Michael Buckley, which takes readers behind the scenes and into the stories of the Brothers Grimm. Sabrina and Daphne Grimm have been shipped off from one foster home to another for many years. What they’re told that their paternal grandmother has agreed to take care of them, though Sabrina becomes very dubious, having heard that the woman died many years ago. However, after meeting the slightly </span>
  <span id="freeText218199034604290422" style="display:none">Needing something a little shorter to fit into my reading schedule, I turned to this series debut by Michael Buckley, which takes readers behind the scenes and into the stories of the Brothers Grimm. Sabrina and Daphne Grimm have been shipped off from one foster home to another for many years. What they’re told that their paternal grandmother has agreed to take care of them, though Sabrina becomes very dubious, having heard that the woman died many years ago. However, after meeting the slightly eccentric woman and seeing family photographs, the girls are more apt to believe these tall tales. The transition from NYC to Ferryport Landing is a shock, though not as much as the truth behind their ancestry. Grimms have long been around to ensure that Everafters are protected, but also abide by all the rules, keeping humans from locking them away. That being said, the form of protection offered is isolating them in their current township and not permitting any further exploration. Surely a factor in all the resentment. Grandma Grimm explained further that she is a form of detective, working to puzzle together some of the odd happenings around Ferryport Landing while also battling the sinister ways of Mayor Charming, once an English prince and now a power-hungry fool. With Sabrina and Daphne on board to help, they come across a house that’s been flattened by what one can only presume is a large boot, beanstalk leaves surrounding the property. The girls watch their grandmother in action as she opens up the investigation and begins positing what might have happened. However, as luck would have it, a giant returns to the scene—large boot and all—where he scoops up Grandmother Grimm, leaving the girls in a sense of panic. A new mystery on their hands—how to retrieve their grandmother—the girls seek the assistance of other Everafters, while dodging some of the more nefarious characters who cross their paths. One can only hope that this will have a happy ending for all. Buckley uses some strong fairytale references, sure to entertain the young adult or teen reader, surely the target audience for this book.<br /><br />Sometimes you need a reading break, but are not fully prepared to turn to the newspaper funny pages. In those cases (or when I need something shorter), I turn to YA books, where I can usually suspend my belief system and yet still be entertained. Buckley provides that here with this first novel in what looks to be a fairly developed series all about the Sisters Grimm and their detective capabilities. Mixing the story of two humans in a community full of Everafters (read: characters from fairytales), Buckley is able not only to provide the reader with some semblance of a connection to previous well-known stories, but also twist the character to suit the story, such as the sheriff who was once one of the three pigs but has since become a corrupted and hoofed authority figure. Buckley seeks not to create fully believed scenarios, but at least entertain with the characters who pepper the pages of this story. The plot is decent for what it is and I was impressed with the flow, keeping the story moving without getting too bogged down in silly humour (though what might be right in line with the age range for the piece). It served its purpose for me and I will try to use the age-appropriate filter here, seeing Neo return to these books in a few years when he is a strong individual reader and criticising my review for being off the mark.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Buckley, for such a wonderful debut piece. I think I may return for more in the future, as there is something fun about these stories.<br /><br />Love/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br />A Book for All Seasons, a different sort of Book Challenge: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/248185-a-book-for-all-seasons">https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/...</a></span>

<div id="review_5208046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5208046" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/175268-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249874214p2/175268.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5208046?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/175268-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">younger fans of Jasper Ffrorde, fans of fractured fairy tales</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175268-bonnie?shelf=mysteries-thrillers">mysteries-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175268-bonnie?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175268-bonnie?shelf=series-in-progress">series-in-progress</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175268-bonnie?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175268-bonnie?shelf=fantasy-sf">fantasy-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5208046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2969181564242832712">This was a playful and fun book, with a few flaws.<br/><br/>Sabrina and Daphne's parents disapear one day out of the blue, and the police can't find them. They bounce from one horrible foster home to another, until an old lady comes forward claiming to be their Grandmother. This is weird, because their parents told them their Grandmother was dead. When they meet her, she tells them that they are descended from The Brother's Grimm, who wrote down true events that occured with real creatures. All of these c</span>
  <span id="freeText2969181564242832712" style="display:none">This was a playful and fun book, with a few flaws.<br /><br />Sabrina and Daphne's parents disapear one day out of the blue, and the police can't find them. They bounce from one horrible foster home to another, until an old lady comes forward claiming to be their Grandmother. This is weird, because their parents told them their Grandmother was dead. When they meet her, she tells them that they are descended from The Brother's Grimm, who wrote down true events that occured with real creatures. All of these creatures have now moved to America, and live in the town that they are now in. It is the Grimm's family job to keep these fairy tale creatures in line, which is a big job.<br /><br />One thing that really bugged me was that the story is told through Sabrina's pov, and she spends the first 100 pages doubting everything and being a brat. I think the story would have been a lot more enjoyable if it had been told through Daphne's pov. She's a sweet girl, and it would have made it a much better story. There are also several flaws. The most glaring one is that the Grimm's, generations ago, bonded the fairy tale creatures to the one town, but the catch was that they bonded themselves there too. If the Grimm's can't leave that town, how did Sabrina and Daphne's father move to NYC, and how did they live there themselves? It's never explained. Another flaw is how many story creatures this town has. Okay, there are the Grimm creatures, and Hans Christian Anderson, and the Wizard of Oz, and Alice in Wonderland, and Shakespeare's Midsummer Night's Dream, but then later on in the story, King Arthur shows up. At some point the author has to draw a line, before it becomes every creature from every story, and not just fairy tale creatures.<br /><br />Overall it was a fun, original, fractured take on the fairy tales. There were jokes that rewarded you for having read the fairy tales, and also from these creatures having to interact with the modern world. The kind of humor you would find in Jasper Fforde's stories, and that I particularly like. It also has a good plot, with a twist at the end that I really didn't expect, which I find very rarely in books on the junior side of the library. On top of that, it's a cute little book, with pages about the size of my hand:) It's a shame that the flaws were so glaring and detracted from an otherwise really cute book. There's a second in the series, and I'm definitely going to read it. I bet it will be a lot more enjoyable now that Sabrina is not doubting everything around her!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2969181564242832712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15116412305543681728"><b>Magic in the wrong hands only leads to chaos.</b><br/><br/>Two orphaned girls discover that they're actually related to the Brothers Grimm, and that that famous book of fairy tales is really a true account of past events. They're also surprised to learn that their grandmother is a fairy tale detective, and she expects them to join her in the crime-solving biz. So, what's their first case? Well, it's a doozy:<br/><br/><b>"I hear they're already trying to rescue their grandmother. Can you believe it?" said the White Rabbit.</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15116412305543681728" style="display:none"><b>Magic in the wrong hands only leads to chaos.</b><br /><br />Two orphaned girls discover that they're actually related to the Brothers Grimm, and that that famous book of fairy tales is really a true account of past events. They're also surprised to learn that their grandmother is a fairy tale detective, and she expects them to join her in the crime-solving biz. So, what's their first case? Well, it's a doozy:<br /><br /><b>"I hear they're already trying to rescue their grandmother. Can you believe it?" said the White Rabbit. "Two kids taking on a giant! The whole family will be pushing up daisies by morning."</b><br /><br />That's right - there's a giant on the loose! Sounds like a job for Jack the Giant-Killer, but first . . . the girls will need to bust him out of prison. <br /><br />This was loads of fun, IF you don't think about it too much. The characters in this enchanted tale come not just from fairy tales, but from all walks of literature. I half expected to run into Pippi Longstocking and Huck Finn. Who know? Maybe they'll show up in some later volumes. There <i>are</i> eight more to go, and I think I'll <i>probably</i> try to read every one of them.<br /><br />It's probably only a three-and-a-half star read, but I'll round up since the author did go to some darker places that I was not expecting.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2307754" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2307754" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75857-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556514715p2/75857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2307754?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/75857-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">infinitely patient fans of Vivian Vande Velde or Jasper Fforde</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2307754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3709075466149966033">Michael Buckley begins this children's series with a compelling premise: The stories of the brothers Grimm and other fairy tale originators (Hans Christian Andersen, etc.) are all true. In a Tolkien-style spin, fairy tale creatures (called "Everafters") used to coexist with humans, but since then they have been exiled to a small town near the suburbs of NYC. The Grimm family is still around, monitoring the Everafters and suspicious crimes in the area.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, this premise offers little com</span>
  <span id="freeText3709075466149966033" style="display:none">Michael Buckley begins this children's series with a compelling premise: The stories of the brothers Grimm and other fairy tale originators (Hans Christian Andersen, etc.) are all true. In a Tolkien-style spin, fairy tale creatures (called "Everafters") used to coexist with humans, but since then they have been exiled to a small town near the suburbs of NYC. The Grimm family is still around, monitoring the Everafters and suspicious crimes in the area.<br /><br />Unfortunately, this premise offers little compensation for having to deal with Sabrina Grimm during the first half of the novel. Recently orphaned under odd circumstances, Sabrina (age 11) and her younger sister are sent to their mysterious grandmother whom the girls were told had died years ago. This all occurs in the first chapter. From there to the halfway point, readers are privy to Sabrina's numerous railings against Granny Grimm proclaiming her as a fraud and a lunatic. <br /><br />After the halfway point, when the author finally lets Sabrina be an effective character instead of her previous killjoy self, the story picks up. Sabrina also becomes tolerable to read about. At times Buckley seems to forget that he is writing a children's novel--perhaps hoping to imitate Jasper Fforde's more effective integration of fictional-characters-as-real-people into his popular Thursday Next novels. This creates scenes that seem incongruously gory, some characters even seeming vicious, especially when, at other points, Buckley seems to be at pains to avoid writing about violence (particularly with the circumstances of the girls' being orphaned). Buckley seems uncertain of his audience and his own style--which changes throughout the narrative.<br /><br />Overall, the story reads more like a setup for future books rather than an actual story that can stand alone. Hopefully, now that Sabrina is out of her funk and the premise is in place, the sisters' future adventures will be more enjoyable to follow.<br /><br />You can find this review and more on my blog <a href="http://www.missprint.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Miss Print</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3709075466149966033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_175958837" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/175958837" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1605591-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252166169p2/1605591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/175958837?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/1605591-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6583994-the-fairy-tale-detectives">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=childrens-fairy-tales">childrens-fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175958837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2126330815907275430">Sabrina Grimm has a few problems:<br/><br/>1. Her parents have disappered.<br/><br/>2. She's the oldest sibling, and we all know what that means.<br/><br/>3. She may or may not have Grandmother, who may or may not be crazy.<br/><br/>4. She isn't a teenager yet, which means she only gets until 9 o'clock.<br/><br/>5. She can't open windows.<br/><br/>6. She had foster parents who were way too partial to lima beans.<br/><br/>7. She knows fashion impaired people.<br/><br/>8. Some boy wants to drown her.<br/><br/><br/>While for children, this book will be enjoyed by adults. The premise is somew</span>
  <span id="freeText2126330815907275430" style="display:none">Sabrina Grimm has a few problems:<br /><br />1. Her parents have disappered.<br /><br />2. She's the oldest sibling, and we all know what that means.<br /><br />3. She may or may not have Grandmother, who may or may not be crazy.<br /><br />4. She isn't a teenager yet, which means she only gets until 9 o'clock.<br /><br />5. She can't open windows.<br /><br />6. She had foster parents who were way too partial to lima beans.<br /><br />7. She knows fashion impaired people.<br /><br />8. Some boy wants to drown her.<br /><br /><br />While for children, this book will be enjoyed by adults. The premise is somewhat similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21326.Fables_Legends_in_Exile__Fables___1_" title="Fables Legends in Exile (Fables, #1) by Bill Willingham" rel="nofollow noopener">Fables: Legends in Exile</a> thought without the heavy symbolism and adult themes. It's true, as some of the reviews have pointed out, that Buckley seems to use a very loose form of fairy tales (and is inspired perhaps by Jasper Fforde and <i>Into the Woods</i>), but the book is amusing and easily accesible by both adults and children.<br /><br />What I like best, however, is Buckley's use of two girls as the "chosen" ones. Too often the chosen one is a boy, and it is nice to see a book where it is two sisters who work together and love each her. As an aside, why do male authors tend to use the female chosen one more than female authors? At least on the children's book level? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33918.China_Mi_ville" title="China Miéville" rel="nofollow noopener">China Miéville</a>, for instance have books where the lead character is a young girl. Okay, true Pratchett had the Johnny Maxwell series, but before that he had <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34507.Equal_Rites__Discworld___3_" title="Equal Rites (Discworld, #3) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Equal Rites</a>. When Rowling set up the next generation of Harry Potter in the epilogue, it was another boy. I find it very intersting.<br /><br />This book as a nice sense of humor, is not too scary, and moves very quickly. Additionally, I was quite impressed by the material at the end (what would be a reading group guide in an adult book). Not only does it include a brief letter from the author, but a brief overview of fairy tales (ie as in terms of literary), suggestions for writing and constructing your own fairy tale, further reading in the form of books and websites, and a brief quiz. All done to teach without looking like they are teaching.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2126330815907275430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText647598902718699613" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“The night is young, and by the grace of magic, so are we.”</i>
</b><br /><br />2 stars, even 2.5 stars at best.<br /><br />Unfortunately this didn't make me feel <i>as</i> young as I should be. In fact, I felt bored and felt like reading this was a bit of a chore, which is sad. Again it might have something to do with reading my previous book at the same time so I pretty much could say, out of the both of them--this one was the lesser. :/<br /><br />Daphne and several characters were the saving graces for me, whereas Sabrina merely dominated the narrative and killed a far bit of the enjoyment for me. Therefore I've dubbed her Sabrina the Joy Killer, much to my distaste. But both sisters were extreme opposites--either one is too engrossed with everything (Daphne &lt;3) or they're so darn septic that they ruin the fun for others (this was Sabrina for me).<br /><br />Other than that the fairytale aspect was really interesting, especially the twist at the end made me smile and laugh a bit. I just wish there was more for me there to enjoy--namely if Sabrina hadn't seemed so negative and whiny throughout the story. Again, I can understand Sabrina's character, it's just how she was presented to us, the readers, was a major turn-off for me on several grounds. x:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“You can't judge the many by the actions of the few.”</b>

<div id="review_36386965" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36386965" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36386965?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fairy tale aficionados</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=middle-grade-juvenile">middle-grade-juvenile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=faerie">faerie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=fairy-tale-theme">fairy-tale-theme</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=brothers-and-sisters">brothers-and-sisters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2013-200s-club-challenge">2013-200s-club-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=paranormal-mystery">paranormal-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=detective-private-eye-sleuth">detective-private-eye-sleuth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=family">family</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36386965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7182879135429296254">The Fairy-Tale Detectives is a pleasant audiobook read that fans of fairy tales (young and those who are young at heart) will probably enjoy. I liked the idea that the Grimms were actually a real family of chroniclers whose legacy continues into the present. Sisters Sabrina and Daphne make for likeable, fun protagonists. I felt for them in that they had lost their parents and were adrift and lacking family and a home. Their grandmother is the kind of gramps you dream of. Although Sabrina was ver</span>
  <span id="freeText7182879135429296254" style="display:none">The Fairy-Tale Detectives is a pleasant audiobook read that fans of fairy tales (young and those who are young at heart) will probably enjoy. I liked the idea that the Grimms were actually a real family of chroniclers whose legacy continues into the present. Sisters Sabrina and Daphne make for likeable, fun protagonists. I felt for them in that they had lost their parents and were adrift and lacking family and a home. Their grandmother is the kind of gramps you dream of. Although Sabrina was very argumentative and hard to deal with at first, it's understandable why. She's acting out because of what she's dealing with. She feels betrayed at her parents' disappearance, and a series of bad foster homes, not to mention the burden of having to protect her younger sister. Daphne was far more likable, but then, she is still in that stage where she's more resilient against the cold, cruel world. I liked Granny Relda and Mr. Canis and of course, their dog Elvis. <br /><br />I liked the inside jokes of the fairy tale characters that are very familiar to those who enjoy the subject. Puck was a lot of fun, and so were the three piggies who are now the law enforcement in town. The author surprised me at the twist on the storyline. I did not expect the direction the story went. It's interesting that I had also read the first graphic novel in the Fables series: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21326.Fables__Vol__1_Legends_in_Exile__Fables___1_" title="Fables, Vol. 1 Legends in Exile (Fables, #1) by Bill Willingham" rel="nofollow noopener">Fables, Vol. 1: Legends in Exile</a>, so I saw some of the same characters with storylines that overlapped in interesting ways. While this is a kids series, I think it has enough nuances that an older reader can enjoy it. <br /><br />Why didn't I rate it higher? I think the narrator and I didn't click very well. I also felt like the story took a while to develop and get interesting, and it never got to that "I have to hear what happens next" phase. Now that doesn't mean I won't continue this series. I'm definitely interested enough to keep going, but this isn't a series I have to read back to back. I'm happy to fill it in amongst other reading adventures. But still, The Fairy Tale Detectives has an interesting concept and appealing characters that do make me want to come back to revisit them in the future.<br /><br />Overall rating: <b>3.5/5.0 stars</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7182879135429296254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/842497624" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/842497624?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780810993228" href="/book/show/295832.The_Fairy_Tale_Detectives">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=youth">youth</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer842497624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9335542073287660993">The best word for this (little) book is "cute" I think. I put it on a shelf I call "youth" as in many ways it's very young and if my kids were small I'd read it to them. On the other hand there are "jokes" or "humorous remarks" that older readers will appreciate. <br/><br/>We start with two "orphans" who have ended up in the care of a dried up lady who dislikes kids but somehow ended up running an orphanage. There have been a chain of....unfortunate foster parents (to use a Lemony Snicketism). Of course t</span>
  <span id="freeText9335542073287660993" style="display:none">The best word for this (little) book is "cute" I think. I put it on a shelf I call "youth" as in many ways it's very young and if my kids were small I'd read it to them. On the other hand there are "jokes" or "humorous remarks" that older readers will appreciate. <br /><br />We start with two "orphans" who have ended up in the care of a dried up lady who dislikes kids but somehow ended up running an orphanage. There have been a chain of....unfortunate foster parents (to use a Lemony Snicketism). Of course that may be a subjective view...do you consider say, psychopaths and such as poor choices for parents?????<br /><br />Oh well.<br /><br />Now the girls, oh did I tell you they were sisters, or their family name? Yes these are the Grimm sisters and they're off to live with their grandmother. The only snag is that the girls parents (before they disappeared of course) had told them their grandparents were dead...<br /><br />Hummm....<br /><br />Well anyway nice book, good story, lots of humor concerning characters you'll recognize. I'll probably read some more of these for light reads when I can use a vacation from reality, seriousness and so on. Enjoy.<br /><br />Now...by the way, I just thought I "mention" that this book was published in 2005. It's about a family named Grimm whose members have to solve mysteries and crimes concerning fairytale creatures that the rest of humanity don't see. They live in <s>Storybrook</s> errrr...."Ferryport Landing" or "Fairyport Landing" where all kinds of fairytale folk live. And can't leave.<br /><br />Then there were a couple of TV shows that came into being in 2011. I'm beginning to wonder if a couple of TV networks might have gotten ideas from....somewhere??????</span>
  <a data-text-id="9335542073287660993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16109321028066903336" style="display:none">My daughter gave this to me and asked me to read it, so of course I did. I mean, even if I don't usually read MG, how do you say no to your super-excited 8 year old telling you she's found a fantastic new book? OBVIOUSLY you read it. She loved it. It was thrilling and exciting and had just the right fright level, and she consumed it about as fast as she's ever read anything. We immediately sought out Book 2 for her.<br /><br />As for me, I enjoyed it--there were twists I didn't see coming, and a couple I did, and a lovely level of humor throughout. And now we have the pleasure of chatting about it together, which is special indeed. So there we go. Give it to your 8 year old, and prepare for a possible buddy read. ;)</span>

<div id="review_20305699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20305699" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/989452-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547795081p2/989452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20305699?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/989452-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">children under twelve, especially girls</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20305699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2016640142069461307">My ten-year-old sister reads all sorts of stuff, and I kind of feel a responsibility to make sure that what she's reading has some literary value. Hence, my discovery of "The Sisters Grimm" series.<br/><br/>My initial reaction was that the style of the writing didn't fit the heftiness of the book itself. Weighing in at almost two hundred pages, I was expecting a little more literary depth. The premise is fun; bringing "fairy tale" characters to life and using two ordinary girls as the protagonists definit</span>
  <span id="freeText2016640142069461307" style="display:none">My ten-year-old sister reads all sorts of stuff, and I kind of feel a responsibility to make sure that what she's reading has some literary value. Hence, my discovery of "The Sisters Grimm" series.<br /><br />My initial reaction was that the style of the writing didn't fit the heftiness of the book itself. Weighing in at almost two hundred pages, I was expecting a little more literary depth. The premise is fun; bringing "fairy tale" characters to life and using two ordinary girls as the protagonists definitely appeals to a lot of young readers. However, the dialogue was a little too cutesy for my taste and I didn't feel the Everafters (Buckley's lingo for "fairy tale" characters) were developed and utilized to their full potential. Maybe later installments in the series will delve more into the lives of the Everafters, but I would have loved to have sat in on a class taught by Snow White, or observed Jack selling his big and tall men's clothing. I think it would have given the one-note "fairy tale" characters more diversity and made the entire book exponentially more interesting.<br /><br />Admittedly, though, I must give the author props for not pandering to grown-ups. I think too many "children's" movies, books, magazines, etc., are geared towards keeping the parents captivated as well as their kids. This is not outstanding writing, and I think when my sister (who loves "The Sisters Grimm") grows up she will realize it...but, as a kid, I think she had every right to enjoy the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2016640142069461307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer16564394388848705718">I LOVED THIS!!!<br/>I knew this was going to include fairytale characters, but this was like a Once Upon a Time for middle grade readers. <br/>There is a town seemingly in the middle of nowhere where these fairytale creatures are stuck. It is up to the Grimm family to keep everyone in line and to solve the mysteries around town. <br/>We meet so many well known characters but with twists on them. We have a glutinous Charming, and a good Big Bad Wolf. Gilda the Good Witch is pretty neutral and the Grimm family i</span>
  <span id="freeText16564394388848705718" style="display:none">I LOVED THIS!!!<br />I knew this was going to include fairytale characters, but this was like a Once Upon a Time for middle grade readers. <br />There is a town seemingly in the middle of nowhere where these fairytale creatures are stuck. It is up to the Grimm family to keep everyone in line and to solve the mysteries around town. <br />We meet so many well known characters but with twists on them. We have a glutinous Charming, and a good Big Bad Wolf. Gilda the Good Witch is pretty neutral and the Grimm family is full of spunk. <br />I couldn't get enough of this. I flew through it since it is pretty action packed. The fun part is solving the mystery but at times I was so caught up in the action, I forgot to consider the clues staring me right in the face. I even did a face palm halfway through this book (I'm not even kidding) because I was like "HOW did I miss THAT?" Great little plot twists thrown in. <br />I was incredibly impressed with the author's creativity and world building. I loved seeing old characters in new lights and loved the mini-feminists that are the Grimm sisters. <br />I immediately went and checked out the 2nd one in the series and can not wait to continue! </span>
  <a data-text-id="16564394388848705718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_117574982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117574982" />
    <a title="Brenda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2197013-brenda"><img alt="Brenda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603310920p2/2197013.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117574982?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda" href="/user/show/2197013-brenda">Brenda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyonewho enjoy fairy tales, and mysteries as well as a good amount of adventure</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2197013-brenda?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117574982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7216454754395484898">I was first attracted to this series by the cover art which is beautifully illustrated by Peter Ferguson and really set the mood of the story with just the right amount of creepiness and gives an accurate image of the two sisters in the story. I loved that the story was dedicated to his grandparents Basil and Relda Gandee and he even used his grandmother’s name in the story. I enjoyed the dark silhouettes of children and fairy tale characters that appear at the beginning of each chapter. It gave</span>
  <span id="freeText7216454754395484898" style="display:none">I was first attracted to this series by the cover art which is beautifully illustrated by Peter Ferguson and really set the mood of the story with just the right amount of creepiness and gives an accurate image of the two sisters in the story. I loved that the story was dedicated to his grandparents Basil and Relda Gandee and he even used his grandmother’s name in the story. I enjoyed the dark silhouettes of children and fairy tale characters that appear at the beginning of each chapter. It gave the book a very vintage feel that really appealed to me. The design of the book with the size and typeface also brought some nice charm to the story. What is interesting about this series is the way in which the fairy tale characters from the stories of Grimm, Hans Christian Anderson, the Wizard of Oz, Alice in Wonderland, and Shakespeare's Midsummer Night's Dream all interact in the town of Ferryport Landing. Michael Buckley changes the way in which you look at classic fairy tales and instead presented a place where the characters are more deceptive. This series will certainly appeal to children who enjoy fairy tales, and mysteries as well as a good amount of adventure. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7216454754395484898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3260326988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3260326988" />
    <a title="Elinor  Loredan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2504970-elinor-loredan"><img alt="Elinor  Loredan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416182317p2/2504970.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3260326988?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elinor  Loredan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elinor  Loredan" href="/user/show/2504970-elinor-loredan">Elinor  Loredan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11543564-the-fairy-tale-detectives">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2504970-elinor-loredan?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3260326988&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3260326988" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4213799584094253846">Classic fairy tale characters are turned upside down in this book. The heroes are villains are jerks and the villains are on the good side. I have to admit I felt a little pain at Beauty and Beast being a bit snotty and at Prince Charming being a royal jerk, but mostly I enjoyed seeing how famous characters would be portrayed--for instance, the Three Little Pigs, Snow White and the Magic Mirror (the storage room inside it is enchanting), and the Big Bad Wolf. As much as I love The Land of Storie</span>
  <span id="freeText4213799584094253846" style="display:none">Classic fairy tale characters are turned upside down in this book. The heroes are villains are jerks and the villains are on the good side. I have to admit I felt a little pain at Beauty and Beast being a bit snotty and at Prince Charming being a royal jerk, but mostly I enjoyed seeing how famous characters would be portrayed--for instance, the Three Little Pigs, Snow White and the Magic Mirror (the storage room inside it is enchanting), and the Big Bad Wolf. As much as I love The Land of Stories Series, some of the beloved characters like Cinderella are a bit flat and boring, while the villains shine as complex, interesting characters. I think making villains dynamic can be much easier than doing the same with "good" characters. <br /><br />Another thing that took off one star is, similarly to The Land of Stories, this book contains characters from stories that I don't consider fairy tales. Yes, Wizard of Oz and Alice in Wonderland contain fairy tale elements, but I don't consider them the same category and I get irritated when authors bring them into books about fairy tales--it seems like a gimmicky move to make. Sticking with the Grimm stories alone would provide plenty of material and make some obscure fairy tales more well-known. <br /><br />Overall, though, a fascinating adventure story full of creativity and surprises. I particularly enjoyed the contrasting personalities of the sisters and how the younger one is in many ways more mature, especially in being diplomatic and empathizing with people. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4213799584094253846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2828103716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2828103716" />
    <a title="Abigail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail"><img alt="Abigail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539121384p2/87835420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2828103716?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abigail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abigail" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail">Abigail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Middle Grade Readers Who Enjoy Fairy-Tale Fiction</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fantasy">childrens-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=fairy-tale-fiction">fairy-tale-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2828103716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2051151782898281911">The first entry in an on-going middle-grade fantasy series, <u>The Fairy-Tale Detectives</u> follows the story of Sabrina and Daphne Grimm, who, after a year and a half in and out of various foster homes, find themselves deposited with the grandmother they had no idea existed. Sabrina, the elder at almost twelve, is naturally distrustful - a characteristic much amplified by more than a year's experience with abusive and/or neglectful adults - and determined to protect the more innocent Daphne. She want</span>
  <span id="freeText2051151782898281911" style="display:none">The first entry in an on-going middle-grade fantasy series, <u>The Fairy-Tale Detectives</u> follows the story of Sabrina and Daphne Grimm, who, after a year and a half in and out of various foster homes, find themselves deposited with the grandmother they had no idea existed. Sabrina, the elder at almost twelve, is naturally distrustful - a characteristic much amplified by more than a year's experience with abusive and/or neglectful adults - and determined to protect the more innocent Daphne. She wants none of this strange Grandma Relda, with her colorful food, mysterious preoccupation with fairy-tale creatures, and somewhat foreboding companion, Mr. Canis; and has no interest in staying in Ferryport Landing, the small forest-enclosed town, on the banks of the Hudson River, to which she and Daphne have come. But when all her preconceived notions - her conviction that Relda Grimm is a fraud and a lunatic, her belief that those stories known as "fairy-tales" are fiction - are utterly destroyed by witnessing a two-hundred-foot-tall giant kidnap Grandma Relda and Mr. Canis, Sabrina swings into action, Daphne at her side. She may have lost one family, when her parents disappeared, but Sabrina Grimm is not the girl to lose a second, now that she's finally found it...<br /><br />I was curious to see how I would like this first entry in Michael Buckley's <i>Sisters Grimm</i> series, as so many of my online friends seem either to dislike it, or, at best, to be ambivalent about it. Although rather strict, in my ideas about what makes a desirable folk or fairy-tale retelling - I prefer faithfulness to the original - I am far more tolerant of works of fantasy fiction that are inspired by various folk traditions, as they are generally not presented as retellings of the original stories themselves. In fact, the overlap between folklore and fantasy is a particular area of interest for me, and something I would like to research. Given that this is so, it's probably not that surprising that I enjoyed <u>The Fairy-Tale Detectives</u> more than some of my fellow reviewers. I liked the <i>idea</i> of it, and I enjoyed many of the details of the story: that Grandma Relda was so colorful, that Mr. Canis (erstwhile Big Bad Wolf) was a reformed character, that Prince Charming was a not-so-charming opportunist, out for number one. I appreciated the fact that the Grimms, and the "Everafter" community that they helped to establish, were relocated to the Hudson Valley, as this seems to offer an oblique commentary on the immigration of so many Germans to this continent, and the safe-haven (however imperfect) it supplied to them. Finally, I really appreciated Sabrina's character, and didn't find her distrust of adults at all unbelievable. Yes, she was rather obnoxious at first, but I would have been far more skeptical and displeased, if she had simply accepted the situation in Ferryport Landing, and learned to trust again, all in an instant. These things take time, and I think Buckley made the right decision, in allowing her distrust to play itself out naturally, only overcome by the evidence of her own senses.<br /><br />All that said, this wasn't a book without flaw, and I did find myself a little impatient with the way Buckley conflated any number of works of fantasy and fairy-tale. If Ferryport Landing was established to house those creatures and beings that the Brothers Grimm - ancestors of our Sabrina and Daphne - encountered through their stories, then the cast of characters should have been limited to the Grimms' fairy-tales. Or, if it was necessary to bring in the work of other fairy-tale authors (Andersen, Perrault) and modern fantasists (Baum, Carroll), then some sort of explanation should have been offered. Perhaps, once established, the town (originally "Fairyport Landing") began to attract other creatures? I also felt that the informative afterword, in the edition I read, was at times misleading, and at times factually inaccurate. Without ever stating this explicitly, Buckley made it seem as if the Brothers Grimm were the first to record fairy-tales, when any reader with even a cursory knowledge of the subject knows that they were preceded by the French salon movement, which was itself inspired by earlier Italian traditions, in the same vein. I was also very frustrated (yet again!), to see the factually incorrect statement that the Chinese variant of <i>Cinderella</i> was the first to be recorded, as the story of the Greek slave girl Rhodopis (see: <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/74143.The_Egyptian_Cinderella" title="The Egyptian Cinderella by Shirley Climo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Egyptian Cinderella</a>
</u>) predates it by more than a millennium.<br /><br />Leaving these issues aside - and they seem to be questions of a more scholarly, rather than literary nature - I did enjoy <u>The Fairy-Tale Detectives</u> enough to want to read subsequent entries in the series. I'm curious to see how Puck's inclusion in the Grimm household will work out, whether Sabrina's trust issues continue, and how the mysterious Red Hand society - could this be a reference to the "Red Hand" of Irish mythology? - comes into all of it. It looks like I will have to track down a copy of <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/295834.The_Unusual_Suspects" title="The Unusual Suspects by Michael Buckley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Unusual Suspects</a>
</u>...</span>
  <a data-text-id="2051151782898281911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edens36" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edens36" href="/user/show/70680590-edens36">Edens36</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2221186264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4847340426339652719">The sister Sabrina and Daphne go through many foster homes, but finnally end up in the house of their grandma grimm. Everything is going just fine for the family other than sabrina thinking grandma Grimm is Crazy, but then she starts to beleive when a giant carries away their grandma. Read the sisters Grimm to find out how they get their grandma back. </span>

<div id="review_321873436" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321873436" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3943494-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465624465p2/3943494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/321873436?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/3943494-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3943494-erin?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3943494-erin?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321873436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12324166136628648429">What really made me pick up this book and read it is the fact that it's about the Grimm's fairy tales. I can't resist anything to do with the Brothers Grimm or fairy tales in general, and this little mystery series was just perfect for what it is. Now I'm not calling it a literary masterpiece, but for 9 and 10 year old girls, this is got to be one of the best series out there.<br/><br/>Despite the fact that most of this series has to do with wild, crazy, fairy tale happenings, the two main characters (Sab</span>
  <span id="freeText12324166136628648429" style="display:none">What really made me pick up this book and read it is the fact that it's about the Grimm's fairy tales. I can't resist anything to do with the Brothers Grimm or fairy tales in general, and this little mystery series was just perfect for what it is. Now I'm not calling it a literary masterpiece, but for 9 and 10 year old girls, this is got to be one of the best series out there.<br /><br />Despite the fact that most of this series has to do with wild, crazy, fairy tale happenings, the two main characters (Sabrina and Daphne) are very solidly grounded in the real world; they have real dreams and fears that any young reader will be able to understand and identify with. Orphaned two years before the story starts, the sisters have been passed from one foster family to another. They rely only on each other, and Sabrina especially feels the weight of keeping them together and safe. Then one day a woman appears claiming to be their grandmother; the problem is their parents told them that their grandmother is dead. Foisted onto this strange old lady, Sabrina and Daphne soon come to learn that family can be a very complicated thing. Dealing with issues of abandonment, siblings, and family, Sabrina and Daphne navigate the rough waters of learning who you are while running from giants.<br /><br />The fairy tale aspect of the story was handled very well. It almost reminds me of Fables by Bill Willingham, but very kid-friendly. Prince Charming is the less-than-honest Mayor of the fairy-tale town. The three little pigs are the police force. Snow White teaches at the school. And Sabrina and Daphne's grandmother is the one surviving Grimm who keeps the whole town in check; and now teach her granddaughters the ways of their family.<br /><br />Filled with action, adventure, heroes and villains, and a great sense of camaraderie and sisterly affection/competition from Sabrina and Daphne, this book was a joy to read from start to finish. A great start to a great series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12324166136628648429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer212538361" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7880565476046322403">Orphans Sabrina (11 year old) and Daphne (7 year old) go to live with their grandmother (who they thought was dead) in the town of Ferryport Landing. After the disappearance of their parents, they go through numerous foster homes. They soon find out that their grandmother is a very strange person who says that the town is filled with fairy-tale beings.<br/><br/>Daphne believes her, Sabrina does not, until their grandmother gets kidnapped by a Giant that is the cause for the destruction in the town. Sabrin</span>
  <span id="freeText7880565476046322403" style="display:none">Orphans Sabrina (11 year old) and Daphne (7 year old) go to live with their grandmother (who they thought was dead) in the town of Ferryport Landing. After the disappearance of their parents, they go through numerous foster homes. They soon find out that their grandmother is a very strange person who says that the town is filled with fairy-tale beings.<br /><br />Daphne believes her, Sabrina does not, until their grandmother gets kidnapped by a Giant that is the cause for the destruction in the town. Sabrina and Daphne, alone in the woods, soon meet Puck (From A Midsummer's Night Dream). He agrees to help them save their grandmother since she was kind to him and fed him sometimes. Sabrina, Daphne, and Puck escape the house on a magic carpet and fly to the Ferryport Landing jail where they rescue Jack (From Jack and the Beanstalk) to kill the giant. <br /><br />So, what happens afterwards, is a mystery for the readers, and I don't want to spoil them the fun. But, during the mystery, they learn something about their parents too - who the girls thought had abandoned them.<br /><br />The book is narrated from Sabrina's point of view. Everyone, who reads this book, will love the character of Daphne - her willingness to believe, the cute kindness and the way she deals with people. I seriously want to read the book from Daphne's side. I think it will be more fun.<br /><br />The author must have given a lot of thought, before coming out with this book. He brings in a lot of characters - from Brother's Grimm, Alice In Wonderland and Shakespeare. The book's mystery has been brought on in a nice way. Good start of the series, considering it as a children's book. ;-)</span>

<div id="review_2097204346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2097204346" />
    <a title="Abigail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56868213-abigail"><img alt="Abigail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597976303p2/56868213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abigail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abigail" href="/user/show/56868213-abigail">Abigail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11543564-the-fairy-tale-detectives">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56868213-abigail?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56868213-abigail?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56868213-abigail?shelf=sibling-love">sibling-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56868213-abigail?shelf=2018-november-reading">2018-november-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2097204346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7467238892754368621"><i> "How did you know that we could get him to do whatever we want if we pretend he's in charge?" Sabrina asked Daphne.<br/>"It's what I do with you," the little girl replied. "You two are exactly the same." </i><br/><br/>Daphne is my fave, okay?<br/><br/>I feel like I read this at the wrong time in life, and it makes me sad. Don't get me wrong, I still love middle-grade, but I get the feeling that if I'd read this book when I was ten or so, I would have LOVED it. I enjoyed it, but I didn't LOVE it. <br/><br/>But it was cute! It's basic</span>
  <span id="freeText7467238892754368621" style="display:none"><i> "How did you know that we could get him to do whatever we want if we pretend he's in charge?" Sabrina asked Daphne.<br />"It's what I do with you," the little girl replied. "You two are exactly the same." </i><br /><br />Daphne is my fave, okay?<br /><br />I feel like I read this at the wrong time in life, and it makes me sad. Don't get me wrong, I still love middle-grade, but I get the feeling that if I'd read this book when I was ten or so, I would have LOVED it. I enjoyed it, but I didn't LOVE it. <br /><br />But it was cute! It's basically "Once Upon a Time" for kids and I'm here for it. Rather than Storybrooke, we have Ferryport Landing, a town where characters from fiction are intermingled with ordinary mortals, but the Everafters cannot leave. The Grimms keep everyone in line, settling disputes and keeping the border intact. But are Sabrina and Daphne Grimm aware of this? No. Doesn't keep the crazy from happening to them, though. <br /><br />I love the way the author put together Ferryport Landing. The characters he worked in are fascinating and original and the twists he put on all of them. Jack the Giant-Killer and Mirror and Mayor Charming and Glinda the Good Witch and ahh it was just really cool. <br /><br />Unfortunately it wasn't my favorite. I didn't like Sabrina all that much. She was something of a season one Emma Swan but not redeemed quickly enough for my liking. Idk, she just kind of annoyed me? But Daphne! and their grandma! and Canis!! Yeah I liked them a lot.<br /><br />Anyway... 3.5 stars from me! Should I keep going? Idk? </span>

<div id="review_1084472641" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1084472641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1245428548740563066">Sabrina and Daphne Grimm's parents, their only known family, have disappeared. After a year and a half in and out of foster homes, the girls find out that they have a grandma they've never heard of. They arrive at her house only to be informed that the girls come from a long line of fairy tale "detectives". For the last 200 years, they've been cleaning up magical problems in the town of Ferryport Landing, a town filled with characters from fairy tales and children's literature. The girls have to</span>
  <span id="freeText1245428548740563066" style="display:none">Sabrina and Daphne Grimm's parents, their only known family, have disappeared. After a year and a half in and out of foster homes, the girls find out that they have a grandma they've never heard of. They arrive at her house only to be informed that the girls come from a long line of fairy tale "detectives". For the last 200 years, they've been cleaning up magical problems in the town of Ferryport Landing, a town filled with characters from fairy tales and children's literature. The girls have to figure out whether this woman is really their grandma, and if she is why did their parents keep her a secret? All while figuring out what to do about a giant that's dropped into town from a bean stalk.<br /><br />I thought this was a solid middle grade book that lots of kids will enjoy, especially those who like the TV show Once Upon a Time. In fact, there are enough odd similarities between this book and the show that I want to check which one came first. They're not similarities so large that either one will ruin the other, but just peculiar enough to make me wonder.<br /><br /> I only give it three stars because although I like the idea and thought it was decently executed, I never really got engrossed in the story or invested in the characters. I would still recommend giving it a try if fairy-tale retellings are your thing, but I'm left hoping that the subsequent books in the series will be a bit more engaging. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1245428548740563066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8806887305692419105">3.5 stars<br/><br/>This was a cute book intended for middle graders. Two orphaned sisters are sent to live with their grandmother. They are very suspicious because their parents had told them that their grandparents were dead. They become even more suspicious because the house where their grandmother lives is quite peculiar. It turns out that the sisters are part of the Grimm family and they play a special role in town. <br/><br/>I enjoyed listening to this book. If you like the graphic novel series Fables or watch</span>
  <span id="freeText8806887305692419105" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />This was a cute book intended for middle graders. Two orphaned sisters are sent to live with their grandmother. They are very suspicious because their parents had told them that their grandparents were dead. They become even more suspicious because the house where their grandmother lives is quite peculiar. It turns out that the sisters are part of the Grimm family and they play a special role in town. <br /><br />I enjoyed listening to this book. If you like the graphic novel series Fables or watched "fractured fairy tales" when you were a kid (or Once Upon a Time now), you might want to check it out. The writing is definitely for middle grade, so I know that my husband thought it was too slow, but I enjoyed it as a filler read. One thing that I've found funny is both this and the Fables world is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Prince Charming isn't really a good guy in either universe --- both of these series are written by men so I'm not sure if a man just wanted to bring Prince Charming down a peg ;-)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I will probably continue this series.</span>
